Forum ^6CeljgsV

Asynchronous communication occurs when messages are persisted to be seen later by the receiver.
There are many forms of it and many tools that use this type of communication. The most important
are Emails, where communication can be 1 to 1 or many to many in the case of mailing lists where you can
subscribe/unsubscribe. There are some critiques to mailing, but the biggest of them is inducing stress, some
studies show that checking mail often, like many times during the day, can cause significant
stress in personal and work life. The solution is usually to force yourself to not check it that often
plus trying to subscribe as much as possible only to daily/weekly digests to receive summary mails. ^aC9YFtvT

Another asynchronous communication tool is a discussion forum, it is not too distant from a mailing list, just
more categorised and carried fully on the internet ^fLALusMK

The other important tools are blogs, they can have different configurations. The first is when the
publisher just shares articles, resources, and thoughts with an audience with no extra interactions which
is a more 1 to many type of relations, the other is when the posts have comment sections the
users can interact with, this creates a more many-to-many type of interaction similar to a forum.
Regardless of the form, the owner of the blog usually is a person or organization and the content
usually is published in the form of a diary, however, the tendency is to take more and more of a
publication media format and this has caused concern for founding and publishing  ^9zS5N7du

All these different tools create what we call virtual communities. Thanks to the internet
it is easier than ever to find people that match your interests no matter how unusual
they may be, plus the fact that you are behind a screen and with possibly a pseudonym
you can really be yourself. This is a good thing to always feel like you are part
of something and have a purpose (the role of the in-person communities), but it also creates
risks since people can fake an identity and fool others, although people can
be fooled in person as well. However, Zuckerberg in a conference
said that virtual communities like this are extremely beneficial and should be the trigger
to much stronger in-person communities and relations ^UDO5YIJp

The creation of virtual communities opened up the use of the
web for sharing things. The biggest examples are socials like YouTube
Pinterest or Flicker where you can share your content. Content shared
this way is called user-generated content since people create it and 
when you mix together different types of data, like pictures and coordinates
to represent them on a map like on Flicker, we call it data mashup.
Sharing things on the web is not limited to socials but also to collaborations.
The biggest example of this are Wikis. Wikipedia was born in 2001 from the name
of the airport Hunululu's bus and allows multiple users to collaborate
and gather information on a particular subject. This can allow to have a huge
amount of info available but the drawback is that everyone can contribute
and therefore the content can change quite often, be unreliable and sometimes
plain wrong so you are always recommended to cross-check content coming from
Wikipidia.
Another manifestation of online collaborations are review websites, which are
supposed to gather the judgment of service from the masses and give new
users and idea of what to expect, however often the people that leave
reviews are a minority and not a good representation, plus many leave
a review for the wrong motivations causing the overall feedback to be ureliable.
The last example is crowdsourcing, this is a very interesting phenomenon where people
get together to see something they want, but that does not exist, come to life.
Usually, someone presents a project to the world with a goal of funds to gather,
if people believe in the project they will help it come to life. The biggest
websites for this are Kickstarter and Indiegogo.
All this ties to the concept of wisdom of the crowd ^paUO9QhN

This can allow to have a huge\namount of info available but the drawback is that everyone can contribute\nand therefore the content can change quite often, be unreliable and sometimes\nplain wrong so you are always recommended to cross-check content coming from\nWikipidia.\nAnother manifestation of online collaborations are review websites, which are\nsupposed to gather the judgment of service from the masses and give new\nusers and idea of what to expect, however often the people that leave\nreviews are a minority and not a good representation, plus many leave\na review for the wrong motivations causing the overall feedback to be ureliable.\nThe last example is crowdsourcing, this is a very interesting phenomenon where people\nget together to see something they want, but that does not exist, come to life.\nUsually, someone presents a project to the world with a goal of funds to gather,\nif people believe in the project they will help it come to life. The biggest\nwebsites for this are Kickstarter and Indiegogo.\nAll this ties to the concept of wisdom of the crowd",
